So the MITM can circumvent the CSRF protection. This\n454:             # is true for any HTTP connection, but anyone using HTTPS expects\n455:             # better! For this reason, for https://example.com/ we need\n456:             # additional protection that treats http://example.com/ as\n457:             # completely untrusted. Under HTTPS, Barth et al. found that the\n458:             # Referer header is missing for same-domain requests in only about\n459:             # 0.2% of cases or less, so we can use strict Referer checking.\n460:             try:\n461:                 self._check_referer(request)\n462:             except RejectRequest as exc:\n463:                 return self._reject(request, exc.reason)\n464: \n465:         try:\n466:             self._check_token(request)\n467:         except RejectRequest as exc:\n468:             return self._reject(request, exc.reason)\n469: \n470:         return self._accept(request)\n471: \n472:     def process_response(self, request, response):\n473:         if request.META.get(\"CSRF_COOKIE_NEEDS_UPDATE\"):\n474:             self._set_csrf_cookie(request, response)\n475:             # Unset the flag to prevent _set_csrf_cookie() from being\n476:             # unnecessarily called again in process_response() by other\n477:             # instances of CsrfViewMiddleware. This can happen e.g. when both a\n478:             # decorator and middleware are used. However,\n479:             # CSRF_COOKIE_NEEDS_UPDATE is still respected in subsequent calls\n480:             # e.g. in case rotate_token() is called in process_response() later\n481:             # by custom middleware but before those subsequent calls.\n482:             request.META[\"CSRF_COOKIE_NEEDS_UPDATE\"] = False\n483: \n484:         return response\n485: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c@674eda1c03a3187905f48afee0f15226aa62fdf3/-/blob/django/middleware/csrf.py"}}}

We can do this by\n39:     # passing the key_salt and our base key through a pseudo-random function.\n40:     key = hasher(key_salt + secret).digest()\n41:     # If len(key_salt + secret) > block size of the hash algorithm, the above\n42:     # line is redundant and could be replaced by key = key_salt + secret, since\n43:     # the hmac module does the same thing for keys longer than the block size.\n44:     # However, we need to ensure that we *always* do this.\n45:     return hmac.new(key, msg=force_bytes(value), digestmod=hasher)\n46: \n47: \n48: RANDOM_STRING_CHARS = \"abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyzABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ0123456789\"\n49: \n50: \n51: def get_random_string(length, allowed_chars=RANDOM_STRING_CHARS):\n52:     \"\"\"\n53:     Return a securely generated random string.\n54: \n55:     The bit length of the returned value can be calculated with the formula:\n56:         log_2(len(allowed_chars)^length)\n57: \n58:     For example, with default `allowed_chars` (26+26+10), this gives:\n59:       * length: 12, bit length =~ 71 bits\n60:       * length: 22, bit length =~ 131 bits\n61:     \"\"\"\n62:     return \"\".join(secrets.choice(allowed_chars) for i in range(length))\n63: \n64: \n65: def constant_time_compare(val1, val2):\n66:     \"\"\"Return True if the two strings are equal, False otherwise.\"\"\"\n67:     return secrets.compare_digest(force_bytes(val1), force_bytes(val2))\n68: \n69: \n70: def pbkdf2(password, salt, iterations, dklen=0, digest=None):\n71:     \"\"\"Return the hash of password using pbkdf2.\"\"\"\n72:     if digest is None:\n73:         digest = hashlib.sha256\n74:     dklen = dklen or None\n75:     password = force_bytes(password)\n76:     salt = force_bytes(salt)\n77:     return hashlib.pbkdf2_hmac(digest().name, password, salt, iterations, dklen)\n78: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c@674eda1c03a3187905f48afee0f15226aa62fdf3/-/blob/django/utils/crypto.py"}}}

It checks for CSRF exemption and safe HTTP methods, then orchestrates the validation flow.\\n\\n2. The _check_token() method (lines 349-399) retrieves the CSRF secret and request token, validates their format, and performs the comparison.
